[1] قوله : مؤخّرة الرّحل ؛ المؤخّرةُ بضم الميم ، وسكون الهمزة وكسر الخاء المعجمة : العود الذي في آخر رحل البعير، وهو بفتح الراء، وسكون الحاء، بالفارسية :
بالان شتر.
[٢]قوله : إن انهدمت الكعبة ؛ أي سقط جدرانها ولم تبق إلا العرصة. [٣] قوله : والعياذ بالله ؛ هذه جملة معترضةٌ مشتملة على التَّعوذ بالله من انهدام
الكعبة ؛ لكونه أمراً مستقبحاً.
(٤) قوله : يجوز ؛ يعني إذا صلّى خارج تلك القلعة التي كانت محاطة بالجدران ،
وتوجه إليها جازت صلاته.
(٥) قوله : وهذا حكم عجيب ؛ هذا إيراد على الشافعية، وحاصله : أَنهم لَمَّا صرَّحوا بجواز الصلاة خارج الكعبة على تقدير انهدام جدرانها ، فهِمَ منه أن القبلةَ إِمَّا
Chapter on Prayer in the Ka'bah. [1] (Sahih) therein (are) the obligatory and supererogatory prayers, as mentioned in al-Hidayah, contrary to al-Shafi'i. [4] [0] And mentioned in the books of al-Shafi'i (is) permissibility if one faces the wall of the Ka'bah. His statement: 'Chapter on Prayer in the Ka'bah' — meaning this chapter is about the rulings of prayer in the House of Allah towards which one turns in prayer and around which one circumambulates; it is called al-Ka'bah due to its square shape. [2] His statement: 'Sahih' — because it is established that the Prophet entered the Ka'bah on the day of conquest and prayed two rak'ahs inside as nafl, narrated by al-Bukhari, Muslim, and others. And it is known that there is no difference between obligatory and supererogatory prayers regarding the condition of facing the Ka'bah, except what evidence indicates, and there is no evidence here indicating a difference, so the obligatory prayer is also permissible without doubt. (3) His statement: 'therein' — i.e., in both the obligatory and supererogatory, so nothing of them is permissible inside according to him. Al-Sighnaqi said in al-Nihayah: 'It seems this word was a slip by the writer, for al-Shafi'i holds the permissibility of prayer inside the Ka'bah for both obligatory and supererogatory, as his companions have recorded in their books like al-Wajiz, al-Khulasa, al-Dhakhira, and others. And none of our scholars have also mentioned the disagreement in the books I have like al-Mabsut, al-Asrar, al-Idah, al-Muhit, and commentaries on al-Jami' al-Saghir and others.' [4] His statement: 'And mentioned...' etc.; its purpose is to refute the author of al-Hidayah that he is contrary, as in the books of the Shafi'ites, and they are more knowledgeable about the school of their Imam than others. [0] His statement: 'al-jawaz' — meaning prayer is absolutely permissible inside the Ka'bah on condition that one faces one of the four walls of the Ka'bah. If one faces the door of the Ka'bah, and it is closed, it is permissible, even if one faces the door while it is open, and the height of the threshold is not equal to the back part of the saddle (mu'akhkhar al-rahil), it is not permissible. And in his books also: 'If the Ka'bah collapses (may Allah protect us), prayer is permissible outside it facing towards it, but not permissible inside it unless there is a screen of a tree or a remaining wall in front of him.' And this is a strange ruling because the permissibility of prayer outside it on the supposition of collapse indicates that the qibla is either the ground of the Ka'bah or its air, so it should be permissible inside without the condition that there be something raised in front of him like the back part of the saddle.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is an explanatory commentary on the chapter heading 'Prayer inside the Ka'bah'. It begins by stating the Hanafi ruling that both fard (obligatory) and nafl (supererogatory) prayers are valid (sahih) inside the Ka'bah, citing al-Hidayah. The commentator then notes that al-Hidayah attributes a contrary view to al-Shafi'i, but he cross-checks with Shafi'i sources and finds that their actual position is permissibility when facing a wall of the Ka'bah. He quotes al-Sighnaqi to suggest that al-Hidayah might have misrepresented al-Shafi'i. The commentary then provides the primary proof: the well-known hadith that the Prophet entered the Ka'bah on the day of conquest and prayed two rak'ahs (nafl) inside, reported by Bukhari and Muslim. The argument is that since there is no evidence differentiating fard from nafl in the condition of facing the Ka'bah, fard is also valid by analogy. Following this, the commentator explains the Shafi'i condition for validity: one must face one of the four walls. If facing the door, it is valid only if the door is closed, or if open, the threshold must be at least the height of the back part of a saddle (mu'akhkhar al-rahil), otherwise it is invalid because one is not facing any part of the Ka'bah. The commentator then criticizes a Shafi'i ruling regarding the hypothetical case of the Ka'bah collapsing: they hold that if it collapses, prayer outside facing the site is valid, but prayer inside the empty foundation is not unless there is a screen. This is deemed inconsistent because if the qibla is the ground/air, then inside should be valid without a screen. The commentary thus defends the Hanafi position and points out an internal contradiction in the Shafi'i position.

Key Terms
الكعبة (al-Ka'bah): The sacred House of Allah in Mecca, square-shaped, towards which Muslims face in prayer and around which they perform tawaf.
مؤخّرة الرّحل (mu'akhkhar al-rahil): The back part of the saddle of a camel; used as a standard measurement for the height of the threshold of the Ka'bah's door to determine valid direction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage, what is the ruling of performing fard (obligatory) prayer inside the Ka'bah?
A) It is not valid because only nafl prayer is allowed inside.
B) It is valid, just like nafl prayer, based on the Prophet's action and analogy.
C) It is valid only if one faces the door of the Ka'bah.
D) It is invalid if the Ka'bah is intact, but valid if it is collapsed.

Key Takeaway
Prayer inside the Ka'bah is valid for both fard and nafl according to the Hanafi school, based on the Prophet's action and the absence of any evidence to differentiate.

Prayer Inside the Ka'bah: Qibla and Barrier Requirements
Inter-madhhab dispute on qibla and prayer inside Ka'bah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school does not require a barrier inside the Ka'bah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The qibla includes the ground and airspace of the Ka'bah, so prayer inside without a barrier is valid even with the door open.

The Ka'bah is the qibla for Muslims worldwide, but what exactly constitutes the qibla when one prays inside it? This passage presents a sharp exchange between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafis argue that the qibla encompasses the ground and airspace of the Ka'bah, not just the building. Therefore, they reject the Shafi'i requirement of a screen (sutrah) when the door is open, and they point to an inconsistency in the Shafi'i position regarding prayer on the demolished site.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafis require for prayer inside the Ka'bah when the door is open (threshold height) and what they do not require (no barrier). Also note their view on the qibla after demolition.
The key is their definition of qibla as ground and airspace.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Shafi'i school holds that the qibla is the building itself. Therefore, when the door is open, a barrier at least mu'akhkharat al-rahil high is needed to ensure one is not facing outside. After demolition, they rely on necessity.
The Shafi'i distinction between normal case and necessity is crucial.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'is argue that the qibla is the building, so inside the intact Ka'bah with an open door, a sutrah is required to block the view outside and ensure facing the building's interior.
They also allow prayer on the demolished site because of necessity (no building left).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis object that if the Shafi'is allow prayer on the bare ground after demolition (without a barrier), this proves the qibla is the ground/airspace, not the building. Thus, requiring a barrier inside is inconsistent.
The Shafi'i answer (necessity justifies) is noted but the Hanafis prefer their own consistent view.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical outcome: Hanafis do not require a sutrah inside the Ka'bah even with the door open, provided the threshold is at least mu'akhkharat al-rahil. Shafi'is require a sutrah of at least that height.
This affects the validity of prayer for those following each school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب الصلاة في الكعبة حتى إذا توجه إلى الباب، وهو مفتوح ، ولا يكونُ ارتفاع العتبة بقدر مؤخّرة الرحل لا يجوز وفي كتبه أيضاً : إنه إن انهدمت الكعبة ـ والعياذ بالله ـ يجوز الصلاة خارجها متوجهاً إليها ، ولا يجوز فيها إلا إذا كان بين يديه سترة شجر ، أو بقية جدار ، وهذا حكم عجيب؛ لأنَّ جواز الصلاة خارجها على تقدير الانهدام يدلُّ على أن القبلة إما أرضُ الكعبة، أو هواؤها، فيجب أن يجوز فيها من غير اشتراط أن يكون بين يديه شيء مرتفع مثل مؤخّرة الرحل . صلاته، وإن كان مفتوحاً فإن كان ارتفاع عتبة الكعبة بقدر مؤخّرةِ الرَّحل جازت أيضاً، وإلا فلا ؛ لأنه حينئذ لا يكونُ التَّوجّه إلى شيء من أجزاء الكعبة بل إلى ما هو خارج عنها. قوله : مؤخّرة الرّحل ; المؤخّرةُ بضم الميم ، وسكون الهمزة وكسر الخاء المعجمة : العود الذي في آخر رحل البعير، وهو بفتح الراء، وسكون الحاء، بالفارسية : بالان شتر. قوله : إن انهدمت الكعبة ; أي سقط جدرانها ولم تبق إلا العرصة. قوله : والعياذ بالله ; هذه جملة معترضةٌ مشتملة على التَّعوذ بالله من انهدام الكعبة ; لكونه أمراً مستقبحاً. قوله : يجوز ; يعني إذا صلّى خارج تلك القلعة التي كانت محاطة بالجدران ، وتوجه إليها جازت صلاته. قوله : وهذا حكم عجيب ; هذا إيراد على الشافعية، وحاصله : أَنهم لَمَّا صرَّحوا بجواز الصلاة خارج الكعبة على تقدير انهدام جدرانها ، فهِمَ منه أن القبلةَ إِمَّا أرض الكعبة المحاط بالجدران أو الهواء المتصل منه إلى السماء لا البناء خاصة، فإنه إن كان القبلة بناء الكعبة خاصة لم يجز التَّوجُهُ إلا مجرَّدِ العرصة، وعلى هذا فما وجه اشتراط جواز الصَّلاةِ داخلها، بأن يكون بين يديه شيء مرتفع بقية جدار أو غيره. وأجيب . عنه : بأنَّ القبلة عنده البناء، إلا عند الاضطرار، وهو فقده فحينئذ يكفي التوجه إلى العرصة، وإنما اشترط وجودَ السترة لجواز الصلاة فيها لئلا يكون توجه إلى خارجها ; ولذا اشترط ذلك عند كون الباب مفتوحة.
Book of Prayer, Chapter on Prayer in the Ka'bah. If he faces the door while it is open, and the height of the threshold is not the measure of the back part of the saddle, it is not permissible. And in his books also: If the Ka'bah collapses — Allah forbid — it is permissible to pray outside facing it, but not within [the collapsed area] unless there is in front of him a screen of a tree or the remnant of a wall. And this is a strange ruling; because the permissibility of prayer outside it on the assumption of its collapse indicates that the qibla is either the ground of the Ka'bah or its airspace, so it should be permissible inside without the condition that there be something in front of him raised like the back part of the saddle. His prayer: if [the door] is open, then if the height of the threshold of the Ka'bah is the measure of the back part of the saddle, it is also permissible; otherwise no, because then facing is not toward any part of the Ka'bah but toward what is outside it. His statement: مؤخّرة الرّحل; it is the piece of wood at the back of the camel's saddle, in Persian: بالان شتر. His statement: إن انهدمت الكعبة; meaning its walls fell and only the ground remained. His statement: والعياذ بالله; this is an interjectory sentence seeking refuge with Allah from the collapse of the Ka'bah because it is an ugly thing. His statement: يجوز; meaning if he prays outside that fortress which was surrounded by walls and faces it, his prayer is valid. His statement: وهذا حكم عجيب; this is an objection against the Shafi'is, its gist: when they declared the permissibility of prayer outside the Ka'bah on the assumption of the collapse of its walls, it is understood from that that the qibla is either the ground of the Ka'bah surrounded by walls or the air connected to it towards the sky, not the building alone; because if the qibla is the building of the Ka'bah alone, facing would not be permissible except merely toward the ground. On this, what is the point of stipulating for the permissibility of prayer inside it that there be in front of him something raised like a remnant of a wall or other? And it was answered: The qibla according to him is the building, except in necessity, i.e., its absence; then facing the ground suffices, and he stipulated the existence of a screen for the permissibility of prayer inside so that he would not be facing outside; therefore he stipulated that when the door is open.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i school concerning the qibla for prayer inside the Ka'bah. The Hanafi position is that the qibla includes the ground of the Ka'bah and the airspace above it up to the sky, not just the building itself. Therefore, if one prays inside the Ka'bah facing the door, the prayer is valid only if the threshold is at least the height of the back part of a camel's saddle (about two-thirds of a dhira'), ensuring that the face is directed toward a part of the Ka'bah. If the Ka'bah were demolished, the building is gone, but the ground remains; the Hanafis hold that prayer facing the site is valid because the qibla is the ground and airspace. The commentator objects that the Shafi'is, who consider the qibla to be the building, paradoxically allow prayer outside on the ruined site without a barrier, yet when praying inside with the door open, they require a barrier. The answer is that for the Shafi'is, the building is the qibla, but in necessity (when the building is gone) the ground suffices; the barrier inside is to prevent facing outside inadvertently.

Key Terms
مؤخّرة الرحل (mu'akhkharat al-rahil): The wooden piece at the back of a camel's saddle, used as a measure of height (about 2/3 dhira').
السترة (al-sutrah): An object in front of the worshipper as a screen, such as a tree or wall remnant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The ground and airspace of the Ka'bah
C) The direction of the Black Stone
D) The threshold of the door

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the qibla includes the ground and airspace of the Ka'bah, making prayer inside valid without a barrier even with the door open, provided the threshold is sufficiently high.

Positioning of Follower Inside the Ka'bah: Back-to-Back vs. Back-to-Face
Ruling on congregation positioning inside Ka'bah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible and impermissible positions of a follower relative to the imam inside the Ka'bah, and apply the principle of taqaddum.

Core Idea
The follower must not be ahead of the imam; back-to-back is permissible, but back-to-face invalidates the congregation.

When praying inside the Ka'bah, how should the follower stand relative to the imam? The Hanafi school provides specific guidance to ensure that the follower does not advance beyond the imam. This passage examines two scenarios: one where the follower and imam face opposite walls (back-to-back) and another where the follower faces the same direction as the imam but behind him (back-to-face).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage describes two situations: (1) follower's back to the imam's back (i.e., they face opposite walls), and (2) follower's back to the imam's face (i.e., they face the same direction).
2
Understand the ruling for back-to-back
When the follower and imam face opposite walls (e.g., follower east, imam west), neither is ahead of the other. This is permissible because there is no taqaddum.
3
Understand the ruling for back-to-face
When the follower faces the same direction as the imam but is behind him (so his back is to the imam's face), he is actually ahead of the imam in direction. This constitutes taqaddum, which invalidates the congregation.
Taqaddum means the follower is physically or directionally ahead of the imam.
4
Note the exception for face-to-face without advancement
If the follower and imam face each other without any advancement (e.g., both facing east but follower is to the west of imam), it is permissible but disliked if there is no barrier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ظهره إلى ظهر إمامه ، لا لِمَن ظَهْرُهُ إلى وجهه ، وكره فوقها قوله : إلى ظهر إمامه ; بأن يتوجه المؤتم مثلاً إلى الجدار الشرقي من جدرانها ، والإمام إلى الغربي، أو بالعكس. قوله : لأن هذا ; أي كون ظهره إلى وجهه، بأن يكون وجه كل منهما إلى الجدار الشرقي مثلاً ويكون وجهه كل مواجها إلى الغربي تقدم، وتقدم المؤتم على الإمام لا يجوز، بخلاف الصور الآخر ، مما ليس فيه تقدم، وإن كان وجهه إلى وجهه، نعم يكره ذلك إن كان بلا حائل، كما في «الدر المختار)، وغيره. قوله : وكره ; أي كرة أداءُ الصَّلاة فرضاً كانت أو نفلاً على سقف الكعبة ; لورود النهى عن ذلك مرفوعاً ، أخرجه الترمذي وابن ماجة وغيرهم، وإنما جازت لوجود التوجه، فإنَّ الكعبة هي العرصة والهواء إلى عنان السماء لا البناء فقط، فلا يضرُّ عدمُ التَّوجّه إليه، ولذا تجوزُ الصَّلاةُ إلى جهتها في المواضع العالية المرتفعة عنها.
And if his back is to the back of his imam, not one whose back is to his face; and [prayer] is disliked on top of it. His statement: 'to the back of his imam' — meaning the follower faces the eastern wall while the imam faces the western, or vice versa. His statement: 'because this' — meaning his back being to his face, such that each faces the eastern wall and their faces face the western, that is advancement, and advancement of the follower over the imam is not permissible, unlike other situations where there is no advancement, even if face to face; indeed it is disliked if without a barrier, as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others. His statement: 'and disliked' — i.e., performing prayer, obligatory or supererogatory, on the roof of the Ka'bah is disliked because of the prohibition narrated in marfu' form, reported by al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah and others. It is only permissible because there is facing, for the Ka'bah is the ground and the air to the canopy of the sky, not the building only; so the lack of facing the building does no harm, and therefore prayer is valid facing it from high places above it.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage states two rulings. First, regarding congregation inside the Ka'bah: if the follower and imam stand back-to-back (e.g., one facing east, the other west), it is permissible because neither is ahead of the other. But if the follower's back is to the imam's face (i.e., follower faces the same direction as imam but behind him), that is impermissible because it constitutes advancement of the follower. However, even face-to-face without advancement is disliked if there is no barrier. Second, praying on the roof of the Ka'bah is disliked (makruh) because of a hadith prohibition. It is valid only because the qibla includes the ground and airspace, not just the building; thus facing the direction from the roof is valid, but disliked as a sign of respect.

Key Terms
تقدم (taqaddum): The follower being ahead of the imam in the same direction, which invalidates congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Impermissible (invalid)
D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
The validity of congregational prayer inside the Ka'bah depends on ensuring the follower is not ahead of the imam; back-to-back is permissible, but back-to-face is not.

Prayer on the Roof of the Ka'bah: Valid but Disliked
Ruling on praying on the roof of the Ka'bah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on praying on the roof of the Ka'bah and explain why it is valid but disliked.

Core Idea
Praying on the roof is valid because qibla includes airspace, but it is disliked as a sign of respect.

Is it permissible to pray on the roof of the Ka'bah? While some may think it invalid due to the need to face the Ka'bah, the Hanafi school clarifies that the qibla includes the entire airspace above the Ka'bah, so facing the direction from the roof is valid. However, the practice is disliked (makruh tanzihan) because of a hadith prohibition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that prayer on the roof of the Ka'bah is disliked (makruh).
The Arabic term is 'kariha'.
2
Understand why it is disliked
A hadith (reported by al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah) prohibits praying on the roof, so it is better to avoid it.
The prohibition is not for validity but for respect.
3
Understand why it is still valid
The Ka'bah is the ground and the airspace up to the sky. When on the roof, one still faces the direction of the Ka'bah (the qibla) even though the building itself is not directly faced.
This is based on the Hanafi view that the qibla includes the air column.
4
Apply the general principle
Therefore, praying on high places that are above the Ka'bah is valid because the direction (jihah) is what matters, not the exact building.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ظهره إلى ظهر إمامه ، لا لِمَن ظَهْرُهُ إلى وجهه ، وكره فوقها قوله : إلى ظهر إمامه ; بأن يتوجه المؤتم مثلاً إلى الجدار الشرقي من جدرانها ، والإمام إلى الغربي، أو بالعكس. قوله : لأن هذا ; أي كون ظهره إلى وجهه، بأن يكون وجه كل منهما إلى الجدار الشرقي مثلاً ويكون وجهه كل مواجها إلى الغربي تقدم، وتقدم المؤتم على الإمام لا يجوز، بخلاف الصور الآخر ، مما ليس فيه تقدم، وإن كان وجهه إلى وجهه، نعم يكره ذلك إن كان بلا حائل، كما في «الدر المختار)، وغيره. قوله : وكره ; أي كرة أداءُ الصَّلاة فرضاً كانت أو نفلاً على سقف الكعبة ; لورود النهى عن ذلك مرفوعاً ، أخرجه الترمذي وابن ماجة وغيرهم، وإنما جازت لوجود التوجه، فإنَّ الكعبة هي العرصة والهواء إلى عنان السماء لا البناء فقط، فلا يضرُّ عدمُ التَّوجّه إليه، ولذا تجوزُ الصَّلاةُ إلى جهتها في المواضع العالية المرتفعة عنها.
And if his back is to the back of his imam, not one whose back is to his face; and [prayer] is disliked on top of it. His statement: 'to the back of his imam' — meaning the follower faces the eastern wall while the imam faces the western, or vice versa. His statement: 'because this' — meaning his back being to his face, such that each faces the eastern wall and their faces face the western, that is advancement, and advancement of the follower over the imam is not permissible, unlike other situations where there is no advancement, even if face to face; indeed it is disliked if without a barrier, as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others. His statement: 'and disliked' — i.e., performing prayer, obligatory or supererogatory, on the roof of the Ka'bah is disliked because of the prohibition narrated in marfu' form, reported by al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah and others. It is only permissible because there is facing, for the Ka'bah is the ground and the air to the canopy of the sky, not the building only; so the lack of facing the building does no harm, and therefore prayer is valid facing it from high places above it.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage states two rulings. First, regarding congregation inside the Ka'bah: if the follower and imam stand back-to-back (e.g., one facing east, the other west), it is permissible because neither is ahead of the other. But if the follower's back is to the imam's face (i.e., follower faces the same direction as imam but behind him), that is impermissible because it constitutes advancement of the follower. However, even face-to-face without advancement is disliked if there is no barrier. Second, praying on the roof of the Ka'bah is disliked (makruh) because of a hadith prohibition. It is valid only because the qibla includes the ground and airspace, not just the building; thus facing the direction from the roof is valid, but disliked as a sign of respect.

Key Terms
كره (kariha): Disliked (makruh tanzihan), meaning valid but better not to do.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is prayer on the roof of the Ka'bah considered valid despite the hadith prohibition?
A) Because the hadith is weak
B) Because the qibla includes the airspace above the Ka'bah
C) Because the roof is part of the mosque
D) Because the prohibition only applies to obligatory prayers

Key Takeaway
Prayer on the roof of the Ka'bah is valid because facing the direction (jihah) suffices, but it is disliked due to the hadith prohibition.

Follower Orientation and Praying on the Kaaba Roof: Hanafi Rulings and Proofs
Commentary on two rulings: orientation inside Kaaba and praying on roof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on follower orientation inside the Kaaba and explain the ruling on praying on the roof, applying the Hanafi definition of qibla (arsah + airspace) and evaluating the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A follower whose back faces the imam's face invalidates prayer; praying on the roof is valid but disliked because the Kaaba's airspace is part of the qibla.

This passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah addresses two specific situations around prayer in relation to the Kaaba: the orientation of a follower inside the sacred House, and the permissibility of praying on its roof. The rulings hinge on the definition of qibla and the concept of taqaddum (being ahead of the imam). Let's unpack the legal reasoning and the cross-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage covers two distinct scenarios: (1) the orientation of a follower inside the Kaaba relative to the imam, and (2) praying on the roof of the Kaaba. List them clearly.
Each has its own proof and conditions.
2
Analyze the follower orientation rule
Understand that 'back to back' (e.g., follower faces east, imam west) is valid, but 'back to face' (follower behind imam, both facing same wall) constitutes taqaddum. Explain why taqaddum invalidates the prayer.
Taqaddum means the follower is closer to the qibla wall than the imam, breaking the connection.
3
Examine the rule on praying on the roof
The ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked) but the prayer is valid. Identify the proof: a marfu' hadith prohibiting it, but the Hanafi school interprets the prohibition as indicating dislike, not absolute prohibition.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) so it does not create haram.
4
Understand the Hanafi qibla definition
The Hanafi school defines the qibla as the entire area of the Kaaba (al-arsah) including the airspace up to the heavens. Therefore, facing any part of this area suffices.
This is what allows prayer on the roof without a sutra.
5
Evaluate the Shafi'i dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i defines the qibla as the building itself, so praying on the roof without a sutra would be invalid. The Hanafi response is that the sutra condition is only necessary when the door is open to avoid facing outside; otherwise, the airspace suffices.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Hanafis allow prayer on the roof outright, while Shafi'is require a sutra.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ظهره إلى ظهر إمامه ، لا لِمَن ظَهْرُهُ إلى وجهه ، وكره فوقها. (ولو ظهره إلى ظهر إمامه ، لا لِمَن ظَهْرُهُ إلى وجهه) ؛ لأنَّ هذا تَقَدُّم. ( وكره فوقها) ؛ تعظيما للكعبة ، وفي «الهداية»: إنَّه لا يجوز عند الشافعي . وفي كتبه : أنه لا يجوز إلا أن يكون بين يديه شيء مرتفع. أرض الكعبة المحاط بالجدران أو الهواء المتصل منه إلى السماء لا البناء خاصة، فإنه إن كان القبلة بناء الكعبة خاصة لم يجز التَّوجُهُ إلا مجرَّدِ العرصة، وعلى هذا فما وجه اشتراط جواز الصَّلاةِ داخلها، بأن يكون بين يديه شيء مرتفع بقية جدار أو غيره. وأجيب عنه : بأنَّ القبلة عنده البناء، إلا عند الاضطرار، وهو فقده فحينئذ يكفي التوجه إلى العرصة، وإنما اشترط وجودَ السترة لجواز الصلاة فيها لئلا يكون توجه إلى خارجها ؛ ولذا اشترط ذلك عند كون الباب مفتوحة.
[1] قوله : إلى ظهر إمامه ؛ بأن يتوجه المؤتم مثلاً إلى الجدار الشرقي من جدرانها ، والإمام إلى الغربي، أو بالعكس. [٢] قوله : لأن هذا ؛ أي كون ظهره إلى وجهه، بأن يكون وجه كل منهما إلى الجدار الشرقي مثلاً ويكون وجهه كل مواجها إلى الغربي تقدم، وتقدم المؤتم على الإمام لا يجوز، بخلاف الصور الآخر ، مما ليس فيه تقدم، وإن كان وجهه إلى وجهه، نعم يكره ذلك إن كان بلا حائل، كما في «الدر المختار)، وغيره.
[۳] قوله : وكره ؛ أي كرة أداءُ الصَّلاة فرضاً كانت أو نفلاً على سقف الكعبة ؛ لورود النهى عن ذلك مرفوعاً ، أخرجه الترمذي وابن ماجة وغيرهم، وإنما جازت لوجود التوجه، فإنَّ الكعبة هي العرصة والهواء إلى عنان السماء لا البناء فقط، فلا يضرُّ عدمُ التَّوجّه إليه، ولذا تجوزُ الصَّلاةُ إلى جهتها في المواضع العالية المرتفعة عنها. (٤) قوله : في كتبه أنه ... الخ . الغرض منه الإيراد على صاحب «الهداية» بنقله الخلاف مطلقاً.
And if his back is to the back of his Imam, not for one whose back is to his face. And it is disliked above it. (And if his back is to the back of his Imam, not for one whose back is to his face) because this is being ahead. (And it is disliked above it) as a reverence for the Kaaba. And in Al-Hidayah: Indeed it is not permissible according to Al-Shafi'i. And in his books: that it is not permissible unless there is something raised in front of him. The ground of the Kaaba surrounded by walls or the connected space from it to the sky, not the building specifically. For if the qibla is the building of the Kaaba specifically, then facing is not valid except toward the bare courtyard. And on this, what is the aspect of stipulating the permissibility of prayer inside it, that there be something raised in front of him, like a remaining wall or other? And it was answered: that the qibla according to him is the building, except in necessity, which is its absence; then facing the courtyard suffices. And he only stipulated the existence of a sutra for the permissibility of prayer inside it, lest one face outside it; and therefore he stipulated that when the door is open. [1] His saying: 'to the back of his Imam' means that the follower faces for example the eastern wall of its walls, and the Imam faces the western, or vice versa. [2] His saying: 'because this' means that his back is to his face, such that each of their faces is toward the eastern wall for example and each of their faces is facing the western; that is being ahead, and the follower being ahead of the Imam is not permissible, contrary to other cases where there is no being ahead, even if his face is to his face; yes, it is disliked if there is no barrier, as in Al-Durr Al-Mukhtar and others. [3] His saying: 'and it is disliked' means that performing prayer, whether obligatory or supererogatory, on the roof of the Kaaba is disliked due to the prohibition reported about that as marfu', narrated by Al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah and others. And it is only permissible due to the existence of facing, for the Kaaba is the courtyard and the air up to the heavens, not the building alone, so the lack of facing it does not harm, and therefore prayer is permissible facing its direction in high places elevated from it. (4) His saying: 'in his books that...' etc. The purpose of it is to object to the author of Al-Hidayah by his transmission of the disagreement absolutely.
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn from Al-Wiqayah, covering two rulings: (1) The orientation of a follower praying inside the Kaaba relative to the Imam. The correct ruling is that the follower may have his back to the Imam's back (e.g., one faces east, the other west), but he may not have his back to the Imam's face (e.g., both facing east, but follower behind) because that constitutes 'taqaddum' (being ahead of the Imam), which is invalid. (2) Praying on the roof of the Kaaba is makruh (disliked) out of reverence for the Kaaba, though the prayer itself is valid because one is still facing the Kaaba's airspace which is considered part of the Kaaba. The commentary then engages with the Shafi'i view as reported in Al-Hidayah: Imam Al-Shafi'i considers it impermissible to pray on the roof without a sutra (a barrier before one), because he defines the qibla as the building itself, not the airspace. The Hanafi response is that the qibla is the entire area (al-arsah) including the air above, which is why prayer is valid on the roof; the sutra condition is only to avoid facing outside if the door is open. The footnotes further clarify the meaning of 'back to back' and the hadith evidence for the dislike of praying on the roof.

Key Terms
تقدم (taqaddum): Being ahead of the imam in terms of proximity to the qibla, which invalidates the follower's prayer.
العرصة (al-arsah): The ground area of the Kaaba enclosed by walls; included in the definition of Kaaba for qibla purposes.
السترة (al-sutra): A barrier placed in front of a praying person to prevent passing and to define direction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a follower praying inside the Kaaba whose back is to the imam's face?
A) Valid, because they are both facing the qibla.
B) Not valid, because the follower is ahead of the imam.
C) Disliked (makruh), but valid.
D) Not valid, because the follower is behind the imam.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines the qibla as the entire area of the Kaaba including its airspace, making prayer on the roof valid but disliked, while follower orientation inside requires avoiding taqaddum.

Congregational Prayer Around the Kaaba: When Closer Doesn't Mean Ahead
Ruling on validity of congregational prayer when followers surround Kaaba and some are closer than imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on taqaddum to determine the validity of congregational prayer when followers encircle the Kaaba.

Core Idea
Only a follower on the imam's side who is closer to the Kaaba is considered ahead; other sides are valid.

This passage from the Hanafi tradition addresses a unique scenario: the Kaaba as the qibla, the imam standing on one side, and followers forming a circle around it. The key principle is that 'being ahead' (taqaddum) is defined by direction, not mere proximity. Understanding this distinction prevents a common error in applying the general rule that a follower must not be ahead of the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sides of the Kaaba
The Kaaba has four walls. The imam stands facing one wall. Followers on that same wall are in his direction.
2
Define taqaddum (being ahead)
In this context, being ahead means being closer to the Kaaba than the imam while facing the same wall. This only applies to followers on the imam's wall.
3
Apply to the three other sides
Followers on the other walls, even if physically closer to the Kaaba, are not considered ahead because they face different walls; their prayer is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اقتدوا متحلقين حولها، وبعضُهم أقرب من إمامه إليها جاز لمن ليس في جانبه. اعلم أن للكعبة أربعة جوانب بحسب جدرانها الأربعة، فالواقف في الجانب الذي يكون الإمام فيه ، إذا كان أقرب إليها من الإمام يكون متقدماً على الإمام بخلاف الواقف في الجوانب الثلاثة الأخر، فإن مَن هو أقرب إلى الكعبة لا يكون متقدما على الإمام. قوله : اقتدوا... الخ ؛ حاصلُ المسألة : أنهم صلوا خارجها بجماعة، وقام الإمام بجهةٍ منها والمؤتمونَ متحلّقين حول الكعبة في أطرافها، تجوز صلاة جميعهم، وإن كان بعضهم أقرب إليها من إمامه ؛ لوجود التوجه إلى الكعبة، إلا من كان أقرب من الإمام في جهة توجهه فإنّه لا تجوز صلاته ؛ لأنه تقدم، وكذا تجوز صلاة من اقتدى خارجها بإمام هو فيها ، وكذا العكس كما حققه عبد الغني النابلسي في رسالة «نقض الجعبة في الاقتداء من جوف الكعبة».
They led in prayer while encircling it, and some of them are closer to it than their imam; it is permissible for one not in his side. Know that the Kaaba has four sides according to its four walls. So the one standing on the side in which the imam is, if he is closer to it than the imam, he is ahead of the imam, contrary to the one standing on the other three sides, for whoever is closer to the Kaaba is not ahead of the imam. His saying: 'they led in prayer...' etc.; the summary of the issue: that they prayed outside it in congregation, and the imam stood on one side of it, and the followers encircled the Kaaba around its sides; the prayer of all of them is valid, even if some of them are closer to it than their imam, due to the existence of facing the Kaaba, except the one who is closer than the imam in his direction of facing, for his prayer is not valid because he is ahead. Likewise, the prayer of one who follows outside it with an imam inside it is valid, and likewise the opposite, as verified by Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi in his treatise 'Naqd al-Ja'ba fi al-Iqtida min Jawf al-Ka'ba'.
Source pages p. 391

Commentary
This passage discusses the validity of congregational prayer around the Kaaba when the imam stands on one side and followers surround the Kaaba. The principle is that the follower must not be ahead (mutaqaddim) of the imam. Here, 'ahead' means closer to the Kaaba in the same direction as the imam. For followers on the other three sides, even if they are physically closer to the Kaaba, they are not considered ahead because they are facing a different wall; their qibla is that wall, not the same direction as the imam. Therefore, their prayer is valid. Only the follower on the same side as the imam who is closer is invalid. The commentary of Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulsi extends this to cases where the imam is inside the Kaaba and followers outside, and vice versa, ruling that it is valid as long as the follower is not ahead in the same direction.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in congregational prayer.
تقدم (taqaddum): Being ahead of the imam in proximity to the qibla in the same direction, which invalidates the follower's prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When followers encircle the Kaaba for congregational prayer, what is the ruling for a follower on the opposite side of the Kaaba from the imam, who is standing closer to the Kaaba than the imam?
A) Invalid, because he is closer to the Kaaba than the imam.
B) Valid, because he is not in the same direction as the imam.
C) Disliked (makruh), but valid.
D) Invalid, because he is facing away from the imam.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, 'ahead' (taqaddum) in congregational prayer around the Kaaba is direction-specific: only followers on the imam's side who are closer to the Kaaba are invalid; all others are valid.

Ruling on Congregational Prayer Around the Ka'bah
Ruling with exception and additional case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of prayer when followers are closer to the Ka'bah than the imam, identify the exception, and apply it to different positions around the Ka'bah.

Core Idea
Closer to the Ka'bah does not mean ahead unless on the imam's side.

Can you pray in congregation around the Ka'bah even if you are standing closer to it than the imam? This lesson clarifies a practical scenario for pilgrims and residents in Makkah. The Hanafi school provides a nuanced ruling based on the direction the imam faces, not just physical distance.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling
The author begins by stating that it is permissible (ja'iz) for followers to pray in a circle around the Ka'bah, even if some are physically closer to it than the imam.
This is the starting point – permissibility despite apparent proximity.
2
Identify the exception
The exception is for a follower who is on the same side (jaanib) as the imam and closer to the Ka'bah. Such a person is considered 'ahead' (muttaqaddim) of the imam, invalidating their prayer.
The key is being on the imam's side, not just any side.
3
Apply to the four sides
The Ka'bah has four sides. Only the side where the imam stands matters; the other three sides do not create a problem because the follower is not in front of the imam's direction of prayer.
Imagine the imam at the Black Stone corner; followers on the other three corners are fine.
4
Note the additional ruling
The passage adds, as verified by Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulusi, that it is also permissible for a follower outside the Ka'bah to follow an imam inside, and vice versa.
This expands the ruling to cover different positions relative to the Ka'bah structure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة باب الصلاة في الكعبة
اقتدوا متحلقين حولها، وبعضُهم أقرب من إمامه إليها جاز لمن ليس في جانبه (اقتدوا متحلقين حولها، وبعضُهم أقرب من إمامه إليها جاز لِمَن ليس في جانيه) ، اعلم أن للكعبة أربعة جوانب بحسب جدرانها الأربعة، فالواقف في الجانب الذي يكون الإمام فيه ، إذا كان أقرب إليها من الإمام يكون متقدماً على الإمام بخلاف الواقف في الجوانب الثلاثة الأخر، فإن مَن هو أقرب إلى الكعبة لا يكون متقدما على الإمام. قوله : اقتدوا... الخ ؛ حاصلُ المسألة : أنهم صلوا خارجها بجماعة، وقام الإمام بجهةٍ منها والمؤتمونَ متحلّقين حول الكعبة في أطرافها، تجوز صلاة جميعهم، وإن كان بعضهم أقرب إليها من إمامه ؛ لوجود التوجه إلى الكعبة، إلا من كان أقرب من الإمام في جهة توجهه فإنّه لا تجوز صلاته ؛ لأنه تقدم، وكذا تجوز صلاة من اقتدى خارجها بإمام هو فيها ، وكذا العكس كما حققه عبد الغني النابلسي في رسالة «نقض الجعبة في الاقتداء من جوف الكعبة».

They followed [the imam] while encircling around it, and some of them are closer to it than their imam; it is permissible for those who are not on his side. Know that the Ka'bah has four sides according to its four walls. So the one standing on the side where the imam is, if he is closer to it than the imam, he becomes ahead of the imam, unlike the one standing on the other three sides, for the one who is closer to the Ka'bah does not become ahead of the imam. His statement: 'they followed...' etc.; the gist of the issue is that they prayed outside it in congregation, the imam stood on one side of it, and the followers were encircling around the Ka'bah on its peripheries. The prayer of all of them is permissible even if some of them are closer to it than their imam, due to facing the Ka'bah, except for the one who is closer than the imam in the direction he faces, for his prayer is not permissible because he is ahead. Similarly, the prayer of one who follows an imam outside while the imam is inside it is permissible, and likewise the opposite, as verified by Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulusi in his treatise 'Naqd al-Ju'bah fi al-Iqtida' min Jawf al-Ka'bah'.

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling of congregational prayer performed around the Ka'bah. The author explains that the Ka'bah has four sides. When the imam stands on one side and the followers encircle the Ka'bah, those on the other three sides may be physically closer to the Ka'bah than the imam, yet this does not invalidate their prayer because they are not ahead of the imam in the direction of prayer. The only exception is a follower who is on the same side as the imam and closer to the Ka'bah; such a person is considered ahead of the imam, and their prayer is not valid. The author also notes that it is permissible for a follower outside the Ka'bah to follow an imam inside, and vice versa, citing the verification of Abd al-Ghani al-Nabulusi. The underlying principle is that the validity of following the imam depends on not being positioned in front of him in the qiblah direction.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in congregational prayer.
تقدم (taqaddum): Being ahead of the imam in the direction of prayer, which invalidates the follower's prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) When the follower is on any side and closer to the Ka'bah than the imam.
B) When the follower is on the same side as the imam and closer to the Ka'bah.
C) When the follower is behind the imam on another side.
D) When the follower is equidistant to the Ka'bah as the imam.

Key Takeaway
A follower's prayer around the Ka'bah is valid except when on the imam's side and closer; distance alone does not invalidate.

Measures of Sadaqat al-Fitr: Half a Sa' for Wheat, Full Sa' for Dates and Barley
Ruling on amounts with evidence from Companions and hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required amount of Sadaqat al-Fitr for wheat, raisins, dates, and barley according to the Hanafi school, and explain the evidence from Companion practice and hadith.

Core Idea
For Sadaqat al-Fitr, half a sa' is given from wheat and raisins, but a full sa' from dates and barley.

This passage lays out the specific measures of Sadaqat al-Fitr (fitrana) for different grains and dried fruits according to the Hanafi school. You will learn not only the amounts but also the evidential basis from the practice of the Companions and authentic hadith, as well as an important internal difference within the school regarding raisins.

Guided Path
1
Identify the grains and their measures
Read the opening sentence: from wheat (burr), its flour, saweeq, or raisins give half a sa'; from dates or barley give a full sa'. Note the distinction.
The derivatives (flour, saweeq) follow the ruling of their base grain.
2
Understand the evidence for half sa' for wheat
The author cites the practice of several senior Companions (Umar, Abu Bakr, Ibn Abbas, etc.) and marfu' hadith, acknowledging that some hadith chains are weak but the Companions' consensus (sukut) strengthens the ruling.
This is a key Hanafi proof: practice of the Companions (qawl al-sahabi) when widespread.
3
Understand the evidence for full sa' for dates and barley
The author states that this measure is established from multiple authentic hadith in Bukhari and Muslim, such as the hadith of Ibn Umar.
No weakness in these hadith; they are sahih.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on raisins
The main text says half a sa' for raisins, but the footnote mentions a riwaya from Hasan ibn Ziyad that raisins require a full sa', which later scholars (al-Bahnasi, al-Shurunbulali) deemed stronger and used for fatwa.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school; the mufta bihi is full sa'.
5
Consider the recommendation of quantity and value
The footnote from Majma' al-Anhur suggests it is better to consider both the quantity and the monetary value when giving fitrana from high-value items like wheat/raisins.
This is a practical note for muftis.

Chapter of Sadaqat al-Fitr. It is: from wheat, or its flour, or its saweeq, or raisins: half a sa', and from dates or barley: a sa'. [1] He said: 'or its flour' meaning flour of wheat and its saweeq, for they are from it, so their ruling is its ruling. [2] He said: half a sa': this measure for wheat is established from Umar and it is with him according to al-Tahawi, and from Abu Bakr with him according to al-Bayhaqi, and from Ibn al-Zubayr, Jabir, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, and Abu Hurayra with him according to Abd al-Razzaq. And there are also narrated in that regard marfu' hadith from Abu Dawud, al-Daraqutni, and others, and the chain of some is weak, as al-Zayla'i detailed in Takhrij Ahadith al-Hidayah, but that does not harm after the practice of the senior Companions is established in accordance with it. As for the measure of a sa' for dates and barley, it is established from several hadith compiled in the books of Sunan and other authentic collections. (1) Saweeq: that which is made from wheat, and it is the fine part of flour. See Taj al-Urus (25:480) and al-Ta'liqat al-Mardiyya (p. 213). (2) And they made raisins like dates in the obligation of a sa' from it, and it is the riwaya of al-Hasan from the Imam, and al-Bahnasi and others authenticated it, and in al-Haqa'iq and al-Shurunbulaliyya from al-Burhan, and with it fatwa is given. See al-Durr al-Mukhtar (2:76) and al-Durr al-Muntaqa (1:229). And in Majma' al-Anhur (1:229): it is better to take into account the quantity and value. (3) From Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ prescribed the sadaqa of Ramadan as half a sa' from wheat, or a sa' from barley, or a sa' from dates upon the slave and free, male and female. In Musnad Ahmad (1:351), Sunan al-Daraqutni (2:152), etc. (4) Nasb al-Raya (4:217). (5) Among them: from Ibn Umar: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ prescribed the zakat al-fitr of Ramadan upon the people as a sa' of dates or a sa' of barley upon every free or slave, male or female from the Muslims. In Sahih Muslim (2:677), Sahih al-Bukhari (2:547), etc.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage establishes the obligatory amount of Sadaqat al-Fitr (fitrana) according to the Hanafi school. It begins by stating the rule: from wheat (barley? No, wheat here is 'burr'), its flour, or its saweeq (a fine flour), or raisins, the amount is half a sa'. From dates or barley, it is a full sa'. The commentator explains that flour and saweeq from wheat are treated the same as wheat itself. He then provides the evidential basis for the half sa' measure for wheat, citing the practice of several Companions (Umar, Abu Bakr, Ibn al-Zubayr, Jabir, Ibn Abbas, Ibn Mas'ud, Abu Hurayra) and marfu' hadith, acknowledging that some hadith chains are weak but that the practice of the senior Companions is sufficient. For dates and barley, the full sa' measure is established by well-known authentic hadith (Bukhari, Muslim). A later note clarifies a difference within the Hanafi school: according to a riwaya from Hasan ibn Ziyad, raisins should be a full sa' like dates, and this is the position given for fatwa by later scholars (al-Bahnasi, al-Shurunbulali, etc.), though some say it is better to consider both quantity and value.

Key Terms
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume, approximately 2.5-3 kg depending on the substance. In fitrana, it is the standard unit.
صدقة الفطر (sadaqat al-fitr): The obligatory charity given at the end of Ramadan, also called fitrana.
بر (burr): Wheat (the grain). In the context of fitrana, it specifically means wheat, as opposed to barley (sha'ir).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the established amount for barley in Sadaqat al-Fitr?
A) Half a sa'
B) A full sa'
C) The value equivalent
D) Barley is not specified

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes half a sa' from wheat and its derivatives, and a full sa' from dates and barley, with an intra-madhhab difference that the fatwa position for raisins is a full sa'.

Intention Timing for Ramadan and Absolute Intention
Timing and scope of intention for Ramadan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the latest time for daytime intention in Ramadan and apply the rule that absolute intention is valid.

Core Idea
For Ramadan, intention before legal midday suffices; absolute intention works because Allah's designation overrides.

The intention (niyyah) is a condition for fasting, but its timing can be flexible. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies that if one did not intend at night, he can still intend during the day before the legal midday (ad-dahwah al-kubra). It also explains why an absolute intention—simply intending to fast without specifying Ramadan—is sufficient. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the intra-Hanafi difference on this point.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is fasting Ramadan, which is fard_ayn. The ruling here is about the condition of intention: it must be present before a specific time if not made at night.
Intention is a shart (condition) for the validity of the fast.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites the hadith of Ashura where the Prophet commanded those who had eaten to fast the rest of the day. This shows that an obligatory fast can be intended during the day.
The dalil is a hadith ahad, but it is used as evidence for the permissibility of daytime intention.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'فليتم بقية يومه' indicates that intention can be made after the day has started. Since Ashura was wajib before Ramadan, it establishes the principle for wajib fasts.
The Hanafi school uses this to extend the rule to Ramadan.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Mukhtasar al-Quduri allows intention up to zawal (customary noon), while Al-Jami' al-Saghir and the matn require it before legal midday (ad-dahwah al-kubra). The commentator prefers the earlier deadline.
The mufta bihi is the stricter position: intention before legal midday.
5
Understand absolute intention
An absolute intention (e.g., 'I intend to fast') suffices for Ramadan because Ramadan is specifically designated by Allah. Even if one intends a nafl or another wajib, it counts for Ramadan.
This is based on the principle that Allah's designation overrides the servant's specific intention.

Know that the legal day is from dawn to sunset, so what is intended by ad-dahwah al-kubra is its midpoint. Then the intention must be present in most of the day, and it is required to be before ad-dahwah al-kubra. And in Al-Jami' as-Saghir: 'with intention before half of the day' – meaning before half of the legal day. For a specific day, like fasting Thursday for example, intention before true dawn is valid; rather it is valid with intention from the night, and with intention during the day before its legal half. So if one intended from the night not to fast due to weakness or other reason, then the sun or dawn rose, and then it occurred to him to fast, he may intend from that time and complete his fast. [2] His statement: 'in most of the day' because what applies to most applies to the whole. And the evidence for the permissibility of fasting Ramadan with an intention from the day is what was narrated: that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ commanded a man from Aslam to announce among the people: 'Whoever has eaten, let him fast the rest of his day, and whoever has not eaten, let him fast, for today is the day of Ashura' – recorded by Bukhari and Muslim. And if he intended a supererogatory or another obligatory fast, he has intended the absolute with an added restriction, so what was added is nullified due to Ramadan being designated for the obligatory, and the absolute remains, so the obligatory is valid. Further detail is in the books of usul. So if the faster specifically intends other than Ramadan, how can Ramadan be valid from him? One who performs a specific action and intends something specific, it is considered other. (3) In Sahih al-Bukhari (1:3) and Sahih Ibn Hibban (2:113) and others.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a scholastic commentary (sharh) expanding on the matn regarding the intention (niyyah) for fasting Ramadan. The author first defines the legal day (al-nahar al-shar'i) as extending from dawn (sadiq) to sunset (ghurub), and clarifies that 'ad-dahwah al-kubra' (the larger forenoon) refers to the midpoint of this legal day. For a valid fast, the intention must be present during most of the day and must be made before that midpoint. The passage then cites Al-Jami' al-Saghir which requires intention 'before half of the day' and explains that this half is the legal half (i.e., ad-dahwah al-kubra), not the customary half (zawal/noon). The text notes that for a specific supererogatory fast (like Thursday), intention must be made before true dawn, but for Ramadan, intention can be made from the night or during the day before its legal half. If someone intended not to fast at night but later decides, he may intend at that later time and continue. The commentator provides the ruling's evidence: the hadith of Ashura, where the Prophet ﷺ commanded a companion to announce that anyone who had already eaten should fast the remainder of the day, and those who had not eaten should fast, because it was Ashura. This hadith demonstrates that a valid intention can be made during the day for an obligatory fast (since Ashura was obligatory before Ramadan's legislation). The passage then addresses the ruling of an absolute intention (niyyah mutlaqah) for Ramadan: it is valid even if one does not specify Ramadan as obligatory, because Ramadan is specifically designated by Allah for the fast, overriding any lesser designation. Similarly, if one intends a supererogatory fast or another obligatory fast (like kaffarah), it counts for Ramadan because the added restriction is annulled. However, the author notes a scholarly discussion: the hadith 'Actions are by intentions' suggests that if one specifically intends something else, Ramadan should not be valid. Nevertheless, the validity of an absolute intention is agreed upon. Finally, the passage notes a difference of opinion: Mukhtasar al-Quduri states that intention up to zawal (customary noon) suffices, but the first position (before ad-dahwah al-kubra) is more correct (asahh). The commentator concludes by stating that the relied-upon position is the first.

Key Terms
الضحوة الكبرى (ad-dahwah al-kubra): The larger forenoon, identified as the midpoint of the legal day, i.e., halfway between dawn and sunset.
نصف النهار الشرعي (nisful-nahar al-shar'i): The legally considered half of the day, defined as ad-dahwah al-kubra, not the actual midday (zawal).
نية مطلقة (niyyah mutlaqah): An absolute intention, i.e., intending to fast without specifying the type (e.g. just 'I intend to fast').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the latest time to make an intention for a valid Ramadan fast if one did not intend at night?
A) Before true dawn
B) Before ad-dahwah al-kubra (legal midday)
C) Before zawal (customary noon)
D) Before sunset

Key Takeaway
For Ramadan, intention can be made during the day before legal midday, and an absolute intention suffices because Allah's designation overrides specific designation.

Ruling on Ambiguous Intention in Fasting
Legal ruling with explanatory commentary on ambiguous intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a fast performed with ambiguous intention and apply the distinction between wajib and nafl.

Core Idea
Ambiguous intention in fasting yields a valid nafl if not Ramadan, but never another wajib.

This lesson explores a common scenario: a person wakes up uncertain whether today is Ramadan or not, and forms a vague intention to fast. The Hanafi school provides a detailed ruling that depends on what the day actually turns out to be. Understanding this ruling clarifies the role of intention (niyyah) in differentiating between obligatory and supererogatory fasts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sub-cases
The passage considers two situations: 1) ambiguity between Ramadan and another wajib (e.g., qada); 2) ambiguity between Ramadan and nafl. Students must distinguish these.
2
Apply the rule for Ramadan becoming apparent
If the day turns out to be Ramadan, the fast counts for Ramadan because the general intention becomes specified; the uncertainty is resolved by the fact.
The principle: 'mujmal mutlaq intention suffices when specification is determined externally.'
3
Apply the rule when it is not Ramadan
If it is not Ramadan, the fast cannot count as another wajib (sub-case 1) because wajib requires determination (ta'yin) and certainty (jazm) at the time of intention. Instead, it falls to nafl. In sub-case 2, if the alternative was nafl, the fast is valid as nafl by absolute intention.
For wajib, ta'yin is a condition; for nafl, mutlaq intention suffices.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The Hanafi position is that absolute intention (mutlaq al-niyyah) is valid for any act unless additional conditions are required. For wajib, the conditions are ta'yin and jazm; for nafl, mutlaq is enough.
This principle distinguishes Hanafi fiqh from schools that require ta'yin for all fasts.

فإن ظَهَرَ رمضانيّته كان عنه ، وإلا فنفل فيهما ( فإن ظَهَر رمضانيتُه كان عنه ؛ لوجودِ مطلق النيَّة ، (وإلا فنفل فيهما) : أي فيما قال : وإلا فعن واجب آخر ، وفيما قال، وإلا فعن نفل. أما في الصورة الأُولَى ؛ فلأنه متردد في الواجب الآخر ، فلا يقعُ . مطلق النية ، فيقع عن النفل وفي الثانية ؛ لوجودِ مطلق النية أيضاً. (1) قوله : فإن ظهر ؛ أي فيما إذا صام متردّداً بين صوم رمضان وبين واجب آخر ، أو بين صوم رمضان وبين نفل إن ظهر أنه من رمضان يقعُ صومه عنه ؛ لوجودِ مطلق النية وإلغاء الوصف الزائد بسبب تعينه. (2) قوله : فلا يقع عنه ؛ لأنه يشترط فيه التعيين مع الجزم، وإذا فُقِدَ ذلك بَقِيَ مطلق نية الصوم، وبه يتأدى النفل لا الواجب. (3) قوله : لوجود مطلق النية أيضاً ؛ فإنّه إذا تردد بين الفرض والنفل لم يتعين أحدهما ، فلغا التعيين وبقي الإطلاق.
If its Ramadan-ness becomes apparent, it counts as that; otherwise it is nafl in both cases. (Explanation: If Ramadan-ness becomes apparent, it counts as that, because of the presence of absolute intention. Otherwise it is nafl: meaning in the case where he said 'otherwise it is for another wajib' or 'otherwise it is nafl'. In the first case, because he is uncertain about the other wajib, so it does not count. So absolute intention remains, and it counts as nafl. In the second case, due to the presence of absolute intention as well. (1) His saying: 'If it becomes apparent' means when one fasts with uncertainty between Ramadan and another wajib, or between Ramadan and nafl, if it becomes clear it is Ramadan, his fast counts as that, due to absolute intention and canceling the extra description due to its determination. (2) His saying: 'It does not count for it' because it requires determination with certainty; when that is absent, absolute intention remains, and by it nafl is performed, not wajib. (3) His saying: 'Due to absolute intention as well' because when one is uncertain between fard and nafl, neither is determined, so the determination is nullified and the absolute remains.
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage is a legal ruling with commentary on the effect of ambiguous intention in fasting. It considers a scenario where a person fasts with a general intention that could be for Ramadan or another obligation, or for Ramadan or a supererogatory fast. If it later becomes clear that the day is from Ramadan, the fast is valid for Ramadan because the intention, though ambiguous, becomes specified. If it does not become Ramadan, then the fast is considered nafl in both sub-cases: when the other possibility was another wajib, the fast does not count for that wajib because determination and certainty are required for obligations; it falls to nafl. When the other possibility was nafl, the absolute intention also yields a valid nafl. This ruling is based on the principle that muthlaq intention suffices for a valid act, but additional requirements must be met for wajib.

Key Terms
مطلق النية (mutlaq al-niyyah): A general intention to fast without specifying a particular category (Ramadan, wajib, nafl).
رمضانية (Ramadaniyyah): The quality of being a day of Ramadan.
تعيين (ta'yin): Specifying the intention (e.g., 'I intend to fast tomorrow for Ramadan').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone fasts intending either Ramadan or a make-up (qada) day, and it becomes clear that it is not Ramadan, what is the ruling?
A) The fast is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The fast counts as a make-up (qada) for the missed obligation.
C) The fast counts as a nafl (supererogatory) fast.
D) The fast counts only for the specific day he had in mind.

Key Takeaway
An ambiguous intention in fasting is valid: if it becomes Ramadan, it counts as Ramadan; otherwise it counts as nafl, never as another wajib.

The Lone Moon-Sighter: Obligation and Consequences
Clarifies obligations and consequences for a lone moon-sighter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a lone moon-sighter, apply the principle that kaffarah is prevented by doubt (shubha), and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A lone moon-sighter must act on his own certainty; a judge’s rejection creates doubt that nullifies kaffarah.

This lesson examines the obligations of a person who sights the moon of Ramadan or Shawwal alone, especially when his testimony is rejected by the judge. You will learn why he must fast based on his own sighting, why he cannot break fast on Shawwal without official acceptance, and why breaking the fast incurs only qada but no kaffarah in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a lone person sighting the moon. For Ramadan, fasting is wajib on him based on his own certainty. For Shawwal, continuing to fast is wajib as ihtiyat (precaution).
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse (2:185) is cited for Ramadan: 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it.' For Shawwal, the dalil is the principle of precaution and the hadith requiring two witnesses for iftar.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse's imperative indicates obligation for anyone who has certainty of the month's arrival. The lone observer has certainty through his own sight; thus, fasting is wajib upon him regardless of the judge's acceptance.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that if the lone observer breaks the fast with intercourse, kaffarah is due because he intentionally violated a certain obligation. The Hanafi school says no kaffarah because the judge's rejection creates shubha (doubt).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi; the principle 'al-hududu tudra'u bi al-shubuhat' repels kaffarah when doubt exists. The judge's rejection establishes a legal doubt, so only qada is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(1) البقرة : من الآية ١٨٥ . وإن أفطر قضى وقبل بلا دَعْوَى ولفظ أشهدُ للصوم مع غيم خبرُ فَرْدٍ وإن أفطر قضى) ، ذِكْرُ القضاء فقط ؛ لبيان أنه لا كفارة عليه خلافاً للشَّافِعِي وقبل بلا دَعْوَى" ولفظ أشهدُ للصوم مع غيم " خبر فرد ) 1 ) قوله : أفطر ؛ أي أفسد بعد ما شرع فيه، وكذا إذا لم يشرع فيه. [٤]قوله : مع غيم ؛ بالفتح ؛ أي سحاب ، وكذا دخان أو غبار ونحوه، ما يمنعُ تمام الإبصار. And whoever sees the moon of fasting or breaking fast alone, he fasts, even if his statement is rejected. (4) His saying: 'And whoever sees...' means when a responsible person (sane, adult, Muslim) sees the crescent of Ramadan alone, and testifies before the judge, but the judge rejects his testimony due to a legal reason—his transgression if the sky is overcast, or his error, or lack of complete number. If the sky is clear, he fasts (obligatorily) due to His saying: 'So whoever among you witnesses the month, let him fast it' (Quran 2:185), and he has certainty of its existence through his sight, even if his statement is not accepted for some reason. Similarly, if he sees the crescent of breaking fast and his testimony is not accepted, he does not break fast, but rather fasts as a precaution, because abandoning the fast of Ramadan is more severe than fasting on the day of Eid, and that it is Eid is established only if his sighting is accepted; but since the judge did not accept it, this creates doubt, so precaution is necessary. And if he breaks (the fast), he makes it up. Mention of qada only is to show there is no kaffarah upon him, contrary to al-Shafi'i. And it is accepted without a claim. And the wording 'I testify' for the fast with cloud is a report of a single person. (1) His saying: 'If he breaks' means he invalidates after having started, and similarly if he did not start. (2) His saying: 'Contrary to al-Shafi'i' because he says: kaffarah is obligatory if he invalidates by intercourse, but he broke in Ramadan due to his certainty of sighting. Our argument: since the judge rejected his testimony, this creates doubt about his sighting, and such kaffarah is prevented by doubts. This is in the case of Ramadan, but in the case of breaking fast, there is no kaffarah because it is a day of Eid. (3) His saying: 'Without a claim' means it is not required that someone claim it or that the seer say 'I testify to my sighting' because it is a religious matter, resembling hadith narration. It is not of the rights of people that require claim and testimony. Hence the statement is accepted from those whose testimony is not accepted, such as a single woman, a slave, and one who has been flogged for false accusation (qadhf)—he who accused someone of fornication without proof and was flogged with eighty lashes; his testimony is never accepted in our school, even if he repents. (4) His saying: 'With cloud' (ghaym) means cloud, also smoke or dust, etc., that prevents complete vision. (0) His saying: 'Fard' (single) means one person; it is established that the Prophet ﷺ permitted the testimony of one person for Ramadan, reported by the authors of sunan. In al-Daraqutni with a weak chain: 'The Messenger of Allah ﷺ did not permit for breaking fast except the testimony of two men.'
Source pages p. 503

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with commentary on the situation of a lone moon-sighter. It establishes that a responsible Muslim who sees the moon of Ramadan alone must fast based on his own certainty, even if the judge rejects his testimony. The proof is the Quranic verse (2:185). For the moon of Shawwal, he does not break his fast but continues fasting as a precaution because leaving Ramadan is more severe and the judge's rejection creates doubt. If he breaks the fast (e.g., by intercourse), he must make it up (qada) but there is no kaffarah (expiation), contrary to Imam al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi reasoning is that the judge's rejection creates a shubha (doubt), and kaffarah is prevented by doubts. The passage also clarifies that testimony about moon sighting is accepted without prior legal claim (da'wa), like narrating hadith, and thus can be accepted from persons whose testimony is normally rejected in other matters (e.g., one woman, a slave, or a flogged false accuser). For Ramadan, when the sky is cloudy, the testimony of a single just person is sufficient; for Shawwal, the testimony of two is required as per hadith.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): Doubt that prevents the application of a prescribed punishment or expiation.
إفطار (iftar): Breaking the fast; here referring to the fast of Ramadan by a lone observer.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed or invalidated fast later.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for deliberately breaking a Ramadan fast; in Hanafi, this includes fasting 60 days or feeding 60 poor, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) He must continue fasting as a precaution.
C) He has the option to fast or not.
D) He must repeat his testimony before another judge.

Key Takeaway
A lone moon-sighter must act on his own certainty, and any doubt from official rejection prevents kaffarah.

Actions Requiring Only Qada in Fasting
List of invalidating actions with the ruling 'qada faqat'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which actions in fasting require only qada and explain why kaffarah is not required based on the Hanafi principle of incomplete violation.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, a fast is only invalidated by something entering the body, not exiting, so many actions only require qada, not kaffarah.

This passage lists numerous scenarios where a person's fast becomes invalid but only needs to be made up later. The key distinction is whether the action constitutes a complete deliberate violation (jinaayah) or is due to forgetfulness, mistake, or involuntary factors. Understanding this list helps distinguish between qada-only and cases requiring kaffarah.

Guided Path
1
Categorize the actions
First, classify each listed action into one of three categories: intentional acts with doubt (e.g., eating thinking it's still night), involuntary acts (e.g., vomiting overcome), or non-nutritive entry (e.g., dust, fly).
The unifying factor is that the fast is broken but the violation is incomplete.
2
Identify the common ruling
Note that for all actions, the author states 'qada faqat' (only makeup). This is the constant ruling.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith 'al-fitr mimma dakhala wa laysa mimma kharaja' – breaking the fast is by what enters, not what exits. This is a zanni transmission but its meaning is clear.
The hadith excludes vomiting (exit) from breaking the fast but includes entry of any substance.
4
Analyze wajh al-dalalah
The operative phrase 'mimma dakhala' (from what enters) implies that only intentional entry of nourishment invalidates sufficiently for kaffarah. Involuntary entry or non-nutritive entry breaks the fast but does not trigger expiation.
Kaffarah is tied to a complete, deliberate violation (jinaayah), which is absent in these cases.
5
Note intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad holds that even a little intentional vomiting invalidates and requires qada; Abu Yusuf requires the vomit to fill the mouth. The author follows Abu Yusuf's view.
The list includes 'istqaa' mil'a fihi' (vomiting filling the mouth) aligning with Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو داوى جائفة، أو آمة، فوصل إلى جوفه، أو دماغه، أو ابتلع حصاة، أو حديداً، أو استقاء ملء فيه، أو تسحر، أو أفطر بظنه ليلاً، وهو يوم، أو أكل ناسياً وظن أنه فطره فأكل عمداً، أو جومعت نائمة، أو لم ينو في رمضان كله صوماً ولا فطراً، أو أصبح غير ناو للصوم فأكل، قضى فقط. ولو أكل أو شرب أو جامع ناسياً، أو نام فاحتلم، أو نظر إلى امرأته فأنزل، أو ادهن، أو اكتحل، أو قبل، أو اغتاب، أو غلبه القيء، أو تقياً قليلاً، أو أصبح جنباً، أو صب في إحليله دهن، أو في أذنه ماء، أو دخل غبار، أو دخان، أو ذباب في حلقه، قضى فقط.
Or he treated a penetrating wound, or a head wound that reaches the brain membrane, and it reached his cavity or brain; or he swallowed a pebble or iron; or he intentionally induced vomiting filling his mouth; or he ate suhur (pre-dawn meal) [thinking it was still night]; or he broke his fast thinking it was night while it was day; or he ate forgetfully and thought that had broken his fast so he ate intentionally; or a sleeping woman was engaged in intercourse; or he did not intend for the entire Ramadan either fast or breaking; or he woke up without intention for fasting and then ate intentionally – he only makes up [that day]. And if he ate, drank, or had intercourse forgetfully; or slept and had a wet dream; or looked at his wife and had an ejaculation; or applied oil; or applied kohl; or kissed; or backbit; or was overcome by vomiting; or vomited a little; or woke up in a state of janabah; or oil was poured into his urethra, or water into his ear; or dust, smoke, or a fly entered his throat – he only makes up.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage is a ruling listing actions that invalidate the fast but only require qada (makeup), without kaffarah (expiation). The author first lists cases where the fast is broken due to something entering the body or intentional actions done under mistaken belief, then states 'قضى فقط' (only qada). The second list includes actions done forgetfully, involuntary emissions, and minor non-nutritive entries. The commentary explains that the proof for qada alone is the hadith: 'The fast is broken by what enters, not by what exits' (Ibn Abbas, Ibn Masood, Ali). Kaffarah is not required because complete intentional violation (jinaaya) is not present. There is an intra-Hanafi difference regarding vomiting: Muhammad considers even a little vomiting if intentional as breaking the fast, while Abu Yusuf disagrees unless it fills the mouth. The mufta bihi position is that kaffarah is not due in any of these cases, only qada.

Key Terms
قضى فقط (qada faqat): Only makeup (fasting another day) is required, no expiation.
جائفة (ja'ifah): A wound that reaches the body cavity (jwf).
آمة (ammah): A head wound that reaches the brain membrane (umm al-dimagh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, any action that invalidates the fast without being a complete deliberate violation of entering a nutritive substance requires only qada, not kaffarah.
